<div id="review_590941081" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590941081" />
    <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog"><img alt="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514886578p2/7379751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/590941081?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog">Gitte TotallyBookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer590941081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer546069481504147866">Jointly reviewed on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/19/promise-me-darkness-book-1-by-paige-weaver/'>http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a><br/><br/><b>Jenny:</b> Okay, this is going to be a difficult review. This book was not what I expected at all. It felt like two books in one to me.. I enjoyed the first half but the second part; I have to say lost me. On that note though….I had to find out what happened! I couldn’t put it down and I was drawn to finishing this book. That probably makes no sense Gitte, but I hope you know what I mean.<br/><br/><b>Gitte:</b> I know exactly what you mean Jenny. I really </span>
  <span id="freeText546069481504147866" style="display:none">Jointly reviewed on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/19/promise-me-darkness-book-1-by-paige-weaver/">http://totallybookedblog.com/2013/04/...</a><br /><br /><b>Jenny:</b> Okay, this is going to be a difficult review. This book was not what I expected at all. It felt like two books in one to me.. I enjoyed the first half but the second part; I have to say lost me. On that note though….I had to find out what happened! I couldn’t put it down and I was drawn to finishing this book. That probably makes no sense Gitte, but I hope you know what I mean.<br /><br /><b>Gitte:</b> I know exactly what you mean Jenny. I really enjoyed the first half of the story and I have to say I assumed it was going down one path then suddenly THAT happened and it took a completely unexpected route that floored me, I actually stopped reading and thought, umm what?! I had no idea what was going on or what I was reading; but I kept on because I needed to find out just where it was going and what would happen to our main characters.<br /><br /><b>Jenny:</b> We have Maddie and Ryder. Best friends since childhood. Ryder is the tart about town – putting it about to every girl possible. Maddie is his virginal bff. Maddie has always had strong feelings for Ryder and they have not diminished despite the separation they have experience with Maddie being away at College. Even though he frustrated me at times, I was drawn to Ryder….how could you not love this tattooed bad boy! But….I had issues with him. This guy went back and forth in his emotions with Maddie so much, I wanted to slap him and his indecisiveness gave me whiplash.<br /><br />Their friendship took a change and both sensed their relationship was going to another level. Feelings were being explored between the two.<br /><br /><i>“We’ve always teased each other but this was different. Underneath the flirting lurked something real. Something dangerous. And I wasn’t sure if I could resist it.” - Maddie</i><br /><br />I was so annoyed with Ryder’s actions after Maggie had given herself to him. I got that he had a “never fall in love” rule but really?? Ryder giving her the “we’re just friends” speech after she entrusts him with something so special, well, I would have sent him on his bike! His actions and words just didn’t gel. He would say one thing and do another. I’m not sure how Maddie put up with him.<br /><br /><i>“My heart felt like it was breaking into a million pieces. Pieces that rested in the palm of his hand, easily crushed and easily forgotten” - Maddie.</i><br /><br />You always knew deep down he had intense feelings for her but he just messed her about way too much for my liking.<br /><br /><b>Gitte:</b> So yes, Maddie, I have to say I initially thought oh no the twenty something magical virginal vagina card has been pulled again, my pet peeve if I have to be honest, why is it that virgins are currently the best thing since sliced bread in fiction? Anyway, she was straight and narrow, wanted the khaki wearing straight laced man with manners, no tattoos in sight and driving a BMW. Yet she has always harboured strong feelings of lust and love for her best friend Ryder who is the exact opposite of what she ultimately wants. Ryder is a sexy, heavily tattooed bad arse player. He is a legend with women because of his dangerous attitude and his wild and crazy behaviour. I loved the friendship these two have and as I was reading I was willing them to drop the game they both played and just get together already. Seriously, I agree Jenny, Ryder fought his love for Maggie through the entire story with poor Maggie not knowing where to turn or what was going on. At one stage I thought, enough, I have had enough it’s too much and no person would honestly put up with being treated the way Maggie was by Ryder. It was so frustrating!<br /><br /><i>“…if we tried to make this work, I would just screw it up like I do everything else. Everything I touch turns to crap, Maddie. I can’t let that happen to us. No matter how much I want you, I’m not willing to lose you.” – Ryder</i><br /><br />However, when it was good…it was good.<br /><br /><i>“Ryder was always saving the day. Even my childhood was filled with him rescuing me. My own personal superhero.” – Maddie<br /><br />“You mean everything to me! You always have!” – Ryder</i><br /><br /><b>Jenny:</b> Yep, he was frustrating alright! This book took THAT dramatic twist at about 40% – to say we did not see it coming is an understatement hey Gitte? This became like a whole other book and whilst apocalyptic (do me a huge favor…if you ever get to meet Gitte…ask her to say that word *wink wink*) books aren’t my thing I felt the author did a good job of keeping me interested until the end because I did think it was going to lose me completely but it didn’t, though I have to admit I wasn’t completely invested in the story.<br /><br />The story was well thought out, there was certainly some tense, heart pounding moments throughout and whilst it did take a backseat to the rest of the story unfolding, the underlying love story kept my interest. The change in story forces Ryder to face his feelings whilst dealing with some pretty harrowing situations. We see how human nature can turn evil in the blink of an eye.<br /><br /><i>“With one touch, he took away my fear and left desire in its place” - Maddie</i><br /><br />No, this wasn’t my sort of story but that does not detract at all what a great job the author did, it was purely a personal thing. Fans of this type of romance/suspense with apocalyptic undertones will devour this one.<br /><br /><b>Gitte:</b> Absolutely Jenny, to say we were gobsmacked is an understatement. The sudden intense twist in this story comes completely out of left field side-lining Maggie and Ryder’s story, pushing it to the background really. It became about THAT rather than them. Sure, their story simmered and would rear its head and come to blows every so often but this story became mostly about survival in a world where the reality of the evil one human being can inflict on another is explored.<br /><br />I have to say that this story was really well written, the Author did a great job at keeping me interested and reading despite not being completely convinced that this type of book was for me. My emotions were genuine and I always say, if an Author makes me feel and experiences what the characters are going through then I know the writing is class!<br /><br /><i>“You need to know that I would die for you Maddie….you are my everything…” - Ryder</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="546069481504147866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_592127007" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592127007" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592127007?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine" href="/user/show/12064393-katherine">Katherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592127007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16415067520072302063">Here goes my mini review (full one to come later on the blog:)<br/><br/>Ok, so I started this book like I start most, having no clue what I'm going to encounter and to my relief I was SO happy with this one.<br/><br/>It is a romance, yes, but it is so much more than that! It's about friendships, family, love, struggle and survival in a crumbling society. This book was like a movie in my head, I not only saw it but I lived and breathed the characters.<br/><br/>The drama surrounding the characters is Scary to think about it be</span>
  <span id="freeText16415067520072302063" style="display:none">Here goes my mini review (full one to come later on the blog:)<br /><br />Ok, so I started this book like I start most, having no clue what I'm going to encounter and to my relief I was SO happy with this one.<br /><br />It is a romance, yes, but it is so much more than that! It's about friendships, family, love, struggle and survival in a crumbling society. This book was like a movie in my head, I not only saw it but I lived and breathed the characters.<br /><br />The drama surrounding the characters is Scary to think about it because it could happen in real life.<br /><br />Ryder not only has to struggle with his demons and insecurities but face the challenge of a changing life in a blink of an eye. Become a provider in times of crises and feel worthy of feelings he struggles with.<br /><br />Maddie's life like everyones else's has been torn upside down and she has to cope and come to terms with everything that is happening juggle a life that was not in her or no one's plans amongst coping with feeling for Ryder and his mixed signals.<br /><br />I Truly Enjoyed this story and I NEED 'Promise Me Light' Like NOW!<br /><br />AWESOME READ!<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="16415067520072302063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/597102844?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johanna" href="/user/show/10198457-johanna">Johanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10198457-johanna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10198457-johanna?shelf=alpha-males">alpha-males</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10198457-johanna?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer597102844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14343122674770624572"><b>***3 Mediocre Stars!!***</b><br/><br/><i>What can I say that hasn’t already been said? <br/>This book had a lot of potential to be 5 star worthy.</i> <br/>Unfortunately, Maddie annoyed the crap out of me and Ryder was just so wishy washy, losing me in the process. One minute Ryder is <b>HOT</b> for Maddie, and the next minute he’s being <b>COLD</b>, and distant. I swear his mood swings were giving me <b>WHIPLASH</b>.. Ryder would say sweet things to Maddie once in awhile but his actions would contradict him.. It was just to much at times.<br/><br/>I did ho</span>
  <span id="freeText14343122674770624572" style="display:none"><b>***3 Mediocre Stars!!***</b><br /><br /><i>What can I say that hasn’t already been said? <br />This book had a lot of potential to be 5 star worthy.</i> <br />Unfortunately, Maddie annoyed the crap out of me and Ryder was just so wishy washy, losing me in the process. One minute Ryder is <b>HOT</b> for Maddie, and the next minute he’s being <b>COLD</b>, and distant. I swear his mood swings were giving me <b>WHIPLASH</b>.. Ryder would say sweet things to Maddie once in awhile but his actions would contradict him.. It was just to much at times.<br /><br />I did however, <b>LOVE</b> the apocalyptic storyline, it had a unique twist that didn’t consist of a zombie infested world. It also had a good amount of sex scenes considering she was a <b>VIRGIN</b>.. <br />And surprisingly enough, there were moments in the book were I was caught off guard or not expecting the new turn of events. Which that alone is an accomplishment. Looking forward to reading book 2, but trust me, I wont be rushing to purchase it when it releases...<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_730266800" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730266800" />
    <a title="Dreamer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19081803-dreamer"><img alt="Dreamer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388055893p2/19081803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730266800?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dreamer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dreamer" href="/user/show/19081803-dreamer">Dreamer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730266800" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2350042547902845891"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380764137i/3121064._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>WTF DID I JUST READ?<br/><br/>Is this author trying to insult my intelligence? Because I feel incredibly insulted right now. A little lesson for you guys: EMP's do <b>not</b> work the way it is portrayed in this book. Easy googling will tell you that much.<br/>For one, an EMP would have had to be struck domestically because of America's missile's defense shield. And if it happened in the night as is portrayed in this book, then chances are there would be A LOT of cars working. Why? Because there would tons of cars i</span>
  <span id="freeText2350042547902845891" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380764137i/3121064._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>WTF DID I JUST READ?<br><br>Is this author trying to insult my intelligence? Because I feel incredibly insulted right now. A little lesson for you guys: EMP's do <b>not</b> work the way it is portrayed in this book. Easy googling will tell you that much.<br>For one, an EMP would have had to be struck domestically because of America's missile's defense shield. And if it happened in the night as is portrayed in this book, then chances are there would be A LOT of cars working. Why? Because there would tons of cars in garages, and garages act like faraday cages, protecting the electronic devices therein from the dangers of EMP. (And no, it would not take down a plane and the ground would not shake).<br>Secondly, did this author glaze over the fact that power grids in cities are protected against EMP strikes? From an engineering point of view, there is more energy in bolts of lightening than in EMP blasts, yet they dont shut down cities because we have engineered them to withstand it.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380764138i/3121065.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ignorance was frankly shocking in this story. It disturbed me, and had me facepalming ten million times.<br>The enemies are referred to as "terrorist countries" and never once have we EVER delved into what could possibly spark something this big. In the everyday world, you have to realize through easy research how countries negotiate and keep this world we live in turning, the possibility of ww3 is so unbelievably miniscule. Not just that, but this author brought up countries that would have no possible reason to feud with America, especially when they benefit so greatly by the consumerism of America (ex: China).<br><br>The heroine was another issue altogether. She was the most annoyingly dumb child-girl I've ever had to be in the head of. The internal dialogue in regards to Ryder were repetetive and pointless. Ryder isn't even a badass. So because he has tribal tattoos, gets drunk, f*cks blondes and fights a lot - that makes him a "bad boy"? He sounds more like a douche bag if you asked me. I know absolutely nothing about Ryder either. No idea what his aspirations are, what he likes or dislikes; all we read about is his struggle with Maddie. And <b>everybody</b> revolves around Maddie. We never ever hear much from anyone else. It's just Maddie, Maddie, Maddie. Fml. <br><br>And the idiot that she is, toward the end, made me want to hammer myself in the head repeatedly. *Spoiler ahead* What woman decides to just head to her house with her barely functioning father <b>alone</b>? I mean, the world's gone to shit, she's bumped into enough dangerous situations along the way, WTF would compel her to do this? Why not wait until Gavin came around or SOMETHING?! What a dumbass. Honestly. DUMB.ASS.<br><br>In fact, they were all dumbasses. We have a supposed survivalist man (Ryder's father) who doesn't even have a generator on standby (wow, great survivalism there, bud), and we have four idiots who decide to trek IN THE HEAT OF SUMMER'S DAY at the risk of f*cking heatstroke instead of traveling AT NIGHT when it's cool and there isn't an unforgiving star in the sky roasting you alive. I mean... that's common sense. Also, who in their right minds would sleep in an abandoned minivan in the middle of the road at night? I just... What the...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380764138ra/3121066.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And lastly... The writing was awful. Do you want one fine example? Here it is, folks:<br>"The water was hot from sitting in the garage but it was <b>wet</b>."<br>It was wet, guys. It was wet. Wet. Water was wet and....<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/675444.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2350042547902845891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_638497468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/638497468" />
    <a title="V.J. Chambers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2497416-v-j-chambers"><img alt="V.J. Chambers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388183877p2/2497416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638497468?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="V.J. Chambers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="V.J. Chambers" href="/user/show/2497416-v-j-chambers">V.J. Chambers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2497416-v-j-chambers?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2497416-v-j-chambers?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638497468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11279252624142726558">I thought this would be awesome. (Warning, minor spoilers and swearing, unless goodreads auto-censors?)<br/><br/>To be fair, this is a DNF for me. <br/><br/>Additionally, here I am breaking my rule about trashing other indie authors online. However, I'm doing this an exercise for myself. I enjoy determining what worked and what didn't work for me when I read a book. I use what I find to help me write better books. So I'm only writing this review because I want to explore what did work about the 40% of this book tha</span>
  <span id="freeText11279252624142726558" style="display:none">I thought this would be awesome. (Warning, minor spoilers and swearing, unless goodreads auto-censors?)<br /><br />To be fair, this is a DNF for me. <br /><br />Additionally, here I am breaking my rule about trashing other indie authors online. However, I'm doing this an exercise for myself. I enjoy determining what worked and what didn't work for me when I read a book. I use what I find to help me write better books. So I'm only writing this review because I want to explore what did work about the 40% of this book that I read, even though it had no effing right to work.<br /><br />Okay, for starters, the book is a walking, talking lump of cliches, right? You've got the virgin 21 year old and the asshole boy toy who sleeps around. <br /><br />Oh, but they're best friends from childhood, so that somehow makes it not some Glines/McGuire clone.<br /><br />Hell, Abbi Glines writes better than this chick, and that is not saying much.<br /><br />'Kay, so for some reason, though, it WORKS. Like, it's so stilted and the dialogue is awful and unrealistic and there are seven adverbs on every page and everyone apparently has a constant sore throat, because they are all talking hoarsely. <br /><br />But the sexual tension--while utterly unrealistic--is powerful.<br /><br />So what does the idiot author do?<br /><br />She takes the ONLY thing she has going for her, the will-they/won't-they of Ryder and Maddie, and she has them fuck.<br /><br />And then...<br /><br />Oh, and then Ryder's like, "No, I don't want to date. I don't date girls. I'm the asshole playboy stereotype, remember?"<br /><br />But it's obvious that he actually likes her and is just in denial.<br /><br />Then the WORLD EXPLODES.<br /><br />This was the part I had been hoping for. I was like, yay, there will be danger and tension and excitement.<br /><br />But I found myself skimming, and I stopped reading, because I didn't care about the characters and Ryder and Maddie were practically together at that point, so I wasn't even curious about how the relationship would pan out.<br /><br />How could the author have fixed this?<br /><br />1-Real characters in a believable situation might have garnered my sympathy. Stereotypes? Eh. Let 'em die.<br /><br />2-If you can't manage to make real people (and let's face it, some of the best stories out there feature cardboard cutout characters. I'm a Star Wars fan. I like horror movies. I watched Titanic. You can pull off a good story without great characters.) then, by all means, do not SCREW UP the one decent piece of tension you've got going for you.<br /><br />Listen, would-be romance authors.<br /><br />In a romance novel, they typically have sex AT THE END.<br /><br />If they have sex earlier, their having sex needs to create MORE PROBLEMS.<br /><br />NO TENSION=NO STORY<br /><br />Blah.<br /><br />A book about two people in danger, barely managing to stay alive, who also are attracted to each other, but won't give in to their attraction for some reason or other? That's a plot I NEVER get tired of. <br /><br />They had sex too soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11279252624142726558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BJAVXsiZtrcQr/LX5GhJH6QGu4f9vdBTeLbVEuHUsrsUdy7lLU5wuuyc2bKE6vthw3em2u8+bZrvzM01oF5Rlw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('t2l+otPeouOrrP9NGQU+c34JxobC4lXWaKweeIdkvQCnjkUZNglk7lef1Ch5h4wNGXjb29Bh6B//1gZfxu5eLA==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer133813325356815048">Paige Weaver’s first passion has always been reading. Many hours of her childhood were spent getting lost between the pages of a book, disappearing into other worlds. That turned into a love for writing at a young age. Her first book, Promise Me Darkness, became a New York Times and two time USA Today bestseller.<br/><br/>Paige lives in Texas with her husband and two children. When she's not writing or read</span>
  <span id="freeText133813325356815048" style="display:none">Paige Weaver’s first passion has always been reading. Many hours of her childhood were spent getting lost between the pages of a book, disappearing into other worlds. That turned into a love for writing at a young age. Her first book, Promise Me Darkness, became a New York Times and two time USA Today bestseller.<br /><br />Paige lives in Texas with her husband and two children. When she's not writing or reading, you can find her chasing her kids around and living her very own happily ever-after.<br /></span>
